<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of the United Kingdom.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="16" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/48px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/64px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:United_Kingdom" title="Portal:United Kingdom">United Kingdom&#32;portal</a>  <div class="hlist" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UK_Constituencies_2017_(blank).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/UK_Constituencies_2017_%28blank%29.svg/180px-UK_Constituencies_2017_%28blank%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="335" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/UK_Constituencies_2017_%28blank%29.svg/270px-UK_Constituencies_2017_%28blank%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/UK_Constituencies_2017_%28blank%29.svg/360px-UK_Constituencies_2017_%28blank%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3257" data-file-height="6060" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UK_Constituencies_2017_(blank).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The current UK Parliamentary constituencies.</div></div></div>
<p>The <b>United Kingdom Parliament</b> currently has 650 <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_constituencies" title="United Kingdom constituencies">Parliamentary constituencies</a> across the constituent countries (<a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>), each electing a single <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a> (MP) to the <a href="/wiki/British_House_of_Commons" class="mw-redirect" title="British House of Commons">House of Commons</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Plurality voting system">plurality</a> (<a href="/wiki/First_past_the_post" class="mw-redirect" title="First past the post">first past the post</a>) system of election, ordinarily every five years. <a href="/wiki/Voting" title="Voting">Voting</a> last took place in all 650 of those constituencies at the <a href="/wiki/2017_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2017 United Kingdom general election">United Kingdom general election</a> on 8 June 2017, and these results have been counted and verified.
</p><p>The number of seats rose from 646 at the <a href="/wiki/2005_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2005 United Kingdom general election">2005 general election</a> after <a href="/wiki/Boundary_changes_for_the_2010_United_Kingdom_general_election" class="mw-redirect" title="Boundary changes for the 2010 United Kingdom general election">proposals made</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Boundary_commissions_(United_Kingdom)" title="Boundary commissions (United Kingdom)">boundary commissions for England, Wales and Northern Ireland</a> were adopted through <a href="/wiki/Statutory_instruments" class="mw-redirect" title="Statutory instruments">statutory instruments</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Constituencies in Scotland remained unchanged, as the <a href="/wiki/Boundary_Commission_for_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Boundary Commission for Scotland">Boundary Commission for Scotland</a> had completed a review just before the <a href="/wiki/2005_United_Kingdom_general_election" title="2005 United Kingdom general election">2005 general election</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Primary_legislation" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary legislation">Primary legislation</a> provides for the independence of the boundary commissions for each of the four parts of the UK; the number of seats for each of the countries; permissible factors to use in departing from any old boundaries; and a strong duty to consult. For the 2013 review this was primarily the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Voting_System_and_Constituencies_Act_2011" title="Parliamentary Voting System and Constituencies Act 2011">Parliamentary Voting System and Constituencies Act 2011</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Lagu%C3%AB_method" class="mw-redirect" title="Sainte-Laguë method">Sainte-Laguë formula method</a> is used to form groups of seats split between the four parts of the United Kingdom and the English Regions (as defined by EU Parliament Elections).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The electorate figures given in the second column of the tables below are those as of 2017.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary_of_fundamental_boundary_changes_for_the_2010_general_election">Summary of fundamental boundary changes for the 2010 general election</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom_Parliament_constituencies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Summary of fundamental boundary changes for the 2010 general election">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> – No changes from 2005 election.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> – Number of seats unchanged: three seats were abolished and three were created: <a href="/wiki/Aberconwy_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Aberconwy (UK Parliament constituency)">Aberconwy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arfon_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Arfon (UK Parliament constituency)">Arfon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dwyfor_Meirionnydd_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Dwyfor Meirionnydd (UK Parliament constituency)">Dwyfor Meirionnydd</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> – No extra or fewer seats allocated.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>:</li></ul>
<dl><dd><ul><li><a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warwickshire" title="Warwickshire">Warwickshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derbyshire" title="Derbyshire">Derbyshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norfolk" title="Norfolk">Norfolk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">Essex</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northamptonshire" title="Northamptonshire">Northamptonshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> gained seats. <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Isle of Wight (UK Parliament constituency)">Isle of Wight</a> maintained its status as one constituency, the largest by <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/electorate" class="extiw" title="wikt:electorate">electorate</a>.</li>
<li>The City of <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a> was divided into two seats, neither overlapping part of North Yorkshire.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/North_London" title="North London">North London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> and the metropolitan counties of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear" title="Tyne and Wear">Tyne and Wear</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire" title="South Yorkshire">South Yorkshire</a> lost a seat each.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Herefordshire" title="Herefordshire">Herefordshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Worcestershire" title="Worcestershire">Worcestershire</a>, to reflect their full reinstatement as separate counties, were considered in separate reviews, leading to Herefordshire being split into two simple<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2017)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> constituencies.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bath,_Somerset" title="Bath, Somerset">Bath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a> underwent arguably the most significant changes to reflect the abolition of <a href="/wiki/Avon_(county)" title="Avon (county)">Avon</a>.</li></ul></dd></dl>
<p>Updated electorate figures from December 2010 have been added for the English,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Northern Irish,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Scottish<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and Welsh<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> constituencies.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_area_of_constituencies">Geographical area of constituencies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Kingdom_Parliament_constituencies&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geographical area of constituencies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The constituency with the greatest geographical area in the UK is <a href="/wiki/Ross,_Skye_and_Lochaber_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Ross, Skye and Lochaber (UK Parliament constituency)">Ross, Skye and Lochaber</a>, at about 12,000 square kilometres (4,600&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-parlconst_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parlconst-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The largest in England and Wales is <a href="/wiki/Brecon_and_Radnorshire_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Brecon and Radnorshire (UK Parliament constituency)">Brecon and Radnorshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hansard_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hansard-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The smallest constituency by area is <a href="/wiki/Islington_North_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Islington North (UK Parliament constituency)">Islington North</a> at 7.35 square kilometres (2.84&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-parlconst_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parlconst-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
